This behaviour can be\n107: // changed through options (e.g. WithMax) on creation of the interceptor or on call (through grpc.CallOptions).\n108: //\n109: // Retry logic is available *only for ServerStreams*, i.e. 1:n streams, as the internal logic needs\n110: // to buffer the messages sent by the client. value.\n152: func (c *Client) shouldRefreshToken(err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n153: \tif c.Token != \"\" {\n154: \t\t// do not try to refresh the token as it is set by user\n155: \t\treturn refreshToken(ctx context.Context) error {\n169: \tif c.authTokenBundle == nil {\n170: \t\t// c.authTokenBundle will be initialized only when\n171: \t\t// c.Username != \"\" && c.Password != error.\n330: func isSafeRetry(c *Client, err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n331: \tif isContextError(err) {\n332: \t\treturn false\n333: \t}\n334: \n335: \t// Situation when learner refuses RPC it If revisions waiting to be sent over the\\n56: \\t// watch are compacted, then the watch will be canceled by the server, the\\n57: \\t// client will post a compacted error watch response, and the is \\\"context.Background/TODO\\\", returned \\\"WatchChan\\\" will\\n66: \\t// not be closed and block until event is triggered, except when server\\n67: \\t// returns a non-recoverable error (e.g. ErrCompacted).\\n68: \\t// For example, when context passed with \\\"WithRequireLeader\\\" and the\\n69: \\t// connected server has no leader (e.g. due to network partition),\\n70: \\t// error \\\"etcdserver: no leader\\\" (ErrNoLeader) will be returned,\\n71: \\t// and then \\\"WatchChan\\\" is closed with non-nil \\\"Err()\\\".\\n72: \\t// In order to prevent a watch stream being stuck in a partitioned node,\\n73: \\t// make sure to wrap context with \\\"WithRequireLeader\\\".\\n74: \\t//\\n75: \\t// Otherwise, as long as the context has not been canceled or timed out,\\n76: \\t// watch will retry on other recoverable errors forever until reconnected.\\n77: \\t//\\n78: \\t// TODO: explicitly set context error in the last \\\"WatchResponse\\\" message and close channel?\\n79: \\t// Currently, client contexts are overwritten with \\\"valCtx\\\" that never closes.\\n80: \\t// TODO(v3.4): configure watch retry policy, limit maximum retry number\\n81: \\t// (see https://github.com/etcd-io/etcd/issues/8980)\\n82: \\tWatch(ctx context.Context, key string, opts ...OpOption) WatchChan\\n83: \\n84: \\t// RequestProgress requests a progress notify response be sent The watched events will be returned\n55: \t// through the returned channel. If revisions waiting to be sent over the\n56: \t// watch are compacted, then the watch will be canceled by the server, the\n57: \t// client will post a compacted error watch response, and the channel will close.\n58: \t// If the requested revision is 0 or unspecified, the returned channel will\n59: \t// return watch events that happen after the server receives the watch request.\n60: \t// If the context \"ctx\" is canceled or timed out, returned \"WatchChan\" is closed,\n61: \t// and \"WatchResponse\" from this closed channel has zero events and nil \"Err()\".\n62: \t// The context \"ctx\" MUST be canceled, as soon as watcher is no longer being used,\n63: \t// to release the associated resources.\n64: \t//\n65: \t// If the context is \"context.Background/TODO\", returned \"WatchChan\" will\n66: \t// not be closed and block until event is triggered, except when server\n67: \t// returns a non-recoverable error (e.g. ErrCompacted).\n68: \t// For example, when context passed with \"WithRequireLeader\" and the\n69: \t// connected server has no leader (e.g. due to network partition),\n70: \t// error \"etcdserver: no leader\" (ErrNoLeader) will be returned,\n71: \t// and then \"WatchChan\" is closed with non-nil \"Err()\".\n72: \t// In order to prevent a watch stream being stuck in a partitioned node,\n73: \t// make sure to wrap context with \"WithRequireLeader\".\n74: \t//\n75: \t// Otherwise, as long as the context has not been canceled or timed out,\n76: \t// watch will retry on other recoverable errors forever until reconnected.\n77: \t//\n78: \t// TODO: explicitly set context error in the last \"WatchResponse\" message and close channel?\n79: \t// Currently, client contexts are overwritten with \"valCtx\" that never closes.\n80: \t// TODO(v3.4): configure watch retry policy, limit maximum retry number\n81: \t// (see https://github.com/etcd-io/etcd/issues/8980)\n82: \tWatch(ctx context.Context, key string, opts ...OpOption) WatchChan\n83: \n84: \t// RequestProgress requests a progress notify response be sent in all watch channels.\n85: \tRequestProgress(ctx context.Context) error\n86: \n87: \t// Close closes the watcher and cancels all watch requests.\n88: \tClose() error\n89: }\n90: \n91: type WatchResponse struct {\n92: \tHeader pb.ResponseHeader\n93: \tEvents []*Event\n94: \n95: \t// CompactRevision is the minimum revision the watcher may receive.\n96: \tCompactRevision int64\n97: \n98: \t// Canceled is used to indicate watch failure.\n99: \t// If the watch failed and the stream was about to close, before the channel is closed,\n100: \t// the channel sends a final response that has Canceled set to true with a non-nil Err().\n101: \tCanceled bool\n102: \n103: \t// Created is used to indicate the creation of the watcher.\n104: \tCreated bool\n105: \n106: \tcloseErr error\n107: \n108: \t// CancelReason is a reason of canceling watch\n109: \tCancelReason string\n110: }\n111: \n112: // IsCreate returns true if the event tells that the key is newly created.\n113: func (e *Event) IsCreate() bool {\n114: \treturn e.Type == EventTypePut && e.Kv.CreateRevision == e.Kv.ModRevision\n115: }\n116: \n117: // IsModify }\n121: \n122: // Err is the error value if this WatchResponse holds an error.\n123: func (wr *WatchResponse) Err() error {\n124: \tswitch {\n125: \tcase wr.closeErr != nil:\n126: \t\treturn v3rpc.Error(wr.closeErr)\n127: \tcase wr.CompactRevision != 0:\n128: \t\treturn v3rpc.ErrCompacted\n129: \tcase wr.Canceled:\n130: \t\tif len(wr.CancelReason) != 0 {\n131: \t\t\treturn if the WatchResponse is progress notification.\n139: func (wr *WatchResponse) IsProgressNotify() bool {\n140: \treturn len(wr.Events) == 0 && !wr.Canceled && !wr.Created && wr.CompactRevision == 0 && wr.Header.Revision != 0\n141: }\n142: \n143: // watcher implements the Watcher interface\n144: type watcher struct {\n145: \tremote   pb.WatchClient\n146: \tcallOpts []grpc.CallOption\n147: \n148: Get/Put/Delete, on the other hand, are best suited\n61: \t// for when the operation should be issued at the time of declaration.\n62: \tDo(ctx context.Context, op Op) (OpResponse, error)\n63: \n64: \t// Txn creates a transaction.\n65: \tTxn(ctx context.Context) Txn\n66: }\n67: \n68: type OpResponse struct {\n69: \tput *PutResponse\n70: \tget *GetResponse\n71: \tdel *DeleteResponse\n72: \ttxn *TxnResponse\n73: }\n74: \n75: func (op OpResponse) Put() *PutResponse    { return op.put }\n76: func (op OpResponse) Get() *GetResponse    { return op.get }\n77: func (op OpResponse) Del() *DeleteResponse { return op.del }\n78: func (op OpResponse) Txn() *TxnResponse    { return op.txn }\n79: \n80: func (resp *PutResponse) OpResponse() OpResponse {\n81: \treturn OpResponse{put: resp}\n82: }\n83: \n84: func (resp *GetResponse) OpResponse() OpResponse {\n85: \treturn OpResponse{get: resp}\n86: }\n87: \n88: func (resp *DeleteResponse) OpResponse() OpResponse {\n89: \treturn OpResponse{del: resp}\n90: }\n91: \n92: func (resp *TxnResponse) OpResponse() OpResponse {\n93: \treturn OpResponse{txn: resp}\n94: }\n95: \n96: type kv struct {\n97: \tremote   pb.KVClient\n98: \tcallOpts []grpc.CallOption\n99: }\n100: \n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/etcd-io/etcd@ebf40472ef8515dfa9202eb813b2e9c5dbd035a1/-/blob/client/v3/kv.go%3FL1-100"}}}

\"text\": \"The etcd-io/etcd repository implements comprehensive client-side retry and timeout policy through several coordinated components:\\n\\n## 1. Retry Interceptor (client/v3/retry_interceptor.go)\\nThe core retry logic is implemented via two gRPC client interceptors:\\n- `unaryClientInterceptor`: Handles retry for unary RPC calls (Put, Get, Delete, Txn). It supports configurable maximum retries (defaultUnaryMaxRetries = 100), backoff with jitter, and distinguishes between mutable and immutable operations.\\n- `streamClientInterceptor`: Handles retry for server-side streaming calls. It buffers messages and can reestablish streams on failure. By default, stream retry is disabled (withMax(0)) for safety.\\n- Both interceptors implement exponential backoff via `waitRetryBackoff` and use `backoffLinearWithJitter` for configurable backoff.\\n\\n## 2. Retry Policy Determination (client/v3/retry.go)\\nRetry safety is determined based on operation type and error code:\\n- `isSafeRetryImmutableRPC`: Read operations (Range/Get) can be retried on any transient error (codes.Unavailable). Immutable operations are idempotent.\\n- `isSafeRetryMutableRPC`: Write operations (Put, Delete, Txn) can only be retried when no connection is available (\\\"there is no address available\\\"). This preserves write-at-most-once semantics.\\n- Dedicated retry clients wrap protocol buffer clients: `RetryKVClient`, `RetryLeaseClient`, `RetryClusterClient`, `RetryMaintenanceClient`, and `RetryAuthClient`.\\n\\n## 3. Client Connection and Health Check (client/v3/client.go)\\nThe client initialization flow establishes connections with health verification:\\n- `New()` → `newClient()` → `dialWithBalancer()` → `dial()` creates the connection\\n- `dialSetupOpts()` configures interceptors, keepalive parameters, and TLS credentials\\n- `waitForConnection()` performs health check using gRPC's Health Check API after dialing within the DialTimeout. It disables retry (withMax(0)) to avoid unnecessary delays.\\n- `roundRobinQuorumBackoff()` implements quorum-aware backoff: waits between attempts after cycling through all endpoints\\n- DialTimeout bounds the initial connection establishment time\\n\\n## 4. Endpoint Balancing and Health Management (client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go)\\nThe resolver manages endpoint load balancing:\\n- `EtcdManualResolver`: Manual resolver with round-robin policy configured via gRPC service config\\n- `SetEndpoints()` and `updateState()` dynamically update available endpoints and propagate changes to the gRPC ClientConn\\n- Integrates with gRPC's resolver interface for proper endpoint selection across requests\\n\\n## 5. Watch Implementation (client/v3/watch.go)\\nWatch provides long-lived streaming with resilience:\\n- `watcher` creates multiple `watchGRPCStream` objects for different contexts\\n- `watchGRPCStream` manages a single gRPC Watch stream with reconnection logic:\\n  - Maintains `substreams` map for individual watchers\\n  - `respc` channel receives watch responses\\n  - `errc` channel receives stream errors triggering reconnection\\n  - Implements resuming logic via `resumec` signal\\n- Watch respects caller-provided context but creates an internal `valCtx` that never closes to allow indefinite streaming\\n- Handles server-side cancellation and compaction errors\\n- Uses stream interceptor with retry disabled by default, but individual watch streams handle reconnection internally\\n\\n## 7. \"text\": \"The etcd-io/etcd repository implements comprehensive client-side retry and timeout policy through several coordinated components:\\n\\n## 1. Retry Interceptor (client/v3/retry_interceptor.go)\\nThe core retry logic is implemented via two gRPC client interceptors:\\n- `unaryClientInterceptor`: Handles retry for unary RPC calls (Put, Get, Delete, Txn). It supports configurable maximum retries (defaultUnaryMaxRetries = 100), backoff with jitter, and distinguishes between mutable and immutable operations.\\n- `streamClientInterceptor`: Handles retry for server-side streaming calls. It buffers messages and can reestablish streams on failure. By default, stream retry is disabled (withMax(0)) for safety.\\n- Both interceptors implement exponential backoff via `waitRetryBackoff` and use `backoffLinearWithJitter` for configurable backoff.\\n\\n## 2. Retry Policy Determination (client/v3/retry.go)\\nRetry safety is determined based on operation type and error code:\\n- `isSafeRetryImmutableRPC`: Read operations (Range/Get) can be retried on any transient error (codes.Unavailable). Immutable operations are idempotent.\\n- `isSafeRetryMutableRPC`: Write operations (Put, Delete, Txn) can only be retried when no connection is available (\\\"there is no address available\\\"). This preserves write-at-most-once semantics.\\n- Dedicated retry clients wrap protocol buffer clients: `RetryKVClient`, `RetryLeaseClient`, `RetryClusterClient`, `RetryMaintenanceClient`, and `RetryAuthClient`.\\n\\n## 3. Client Connection and Health Check (client/v3/client.go)\\nThe client initialization flow establishes connections with health verification:\\n- `New()` → `newClient()` → `dialWithBalancer()` → `dial()` creates the connection\\n- `dialSetupOpts()` configures interceptors, keepalive parameters, and TLS credentials\\n- `waitForConnection()` performs health check using gRPC's Health Check API after dialing within the DialTimeout. It disables retry (withMax(0)) to avoid unnecessary delays.\\n- `roundRobinQuorumBackoff()` implements quorum-aware backoff: waits between attempts after cycling through all endpoints\\n- DialTimeout bounds the initial connection establishment time\\n\\n## 4. Endpoint Balancing and Health Management (client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go)\\nThe resolver manages endpoint load balancing:\\n- `EtcdManualResolver`: Manual resolver with round-robin policy configured via gRPC service config\\n- `SetEndpoints()` and `updateState()` dynamically update available endpoints and propagate changes to the gRPC ClientConn\\n- Integrates with gRPC's resolver interface for proper endpoint selection across requests\\n\\n## 5. KV Operations (client/v3/kv.go)\\nKV client wraps the protocol buffer KVClient with call options and error handling:\\n- Implements Put, Get, Delete, Txn operations with `ContextError` wrapper\\n- Calls go through the retry interceptor configured with default call options\\n- Timeout enforcement via context.Context passed from caller\\n\\n## 6. Watch Implementation (client/v3/watch.go)\\nWatch provides long-lived streaming with resilience:\\n- `watcher` creates multiple `watchGRPCStream` objects for different contexts\\n- `watchGRPCStream` manages a single gRPC Watch stream with reconnection logic:\\n  - Maintains `substreams` map for individual watchers\\n  - `respc` channel receives watch responses\\n  - `errc` channel receives stream errors triggering reconnection\\n  - Implements resuming logic via `resumec` signal\\n- Watch respects caller-provided context but creates an internal `valCtx` that never closes to allow indefinite streaming\\n- Handles server-side cancellation and compaction errors\\n- Uses stream interceptor with retry disabled by default, but individual watch streams handle reconnection internally\\n\\n## 7. Lease Implementation (client/v3/lease.go)\\nLease management with automatic keep-alive:\\n- `lessor` implements keep-alive with configurable `firstKeepAliveTimeout` (defaults to 5 seconds)\\n- `KeepAlive()` initiates long-lived stream for lease renewal\\n- `KeepAliveOnce()` performs single renewal with retry support\\n- `stream` multiplexes multiple lease keep-alives over one gRPC stream\\n- Keep-alive deadline management prevents expiration during intervals\\n- Uses `WithRequireLeader` context to prevent split-brain scenarios\\n\\n## 8. Configuration and Options (client/v3/config.go, client/v3/options.go)\\nConfigurable retry and timeout behavior:\\n- Config fields: `DialTimeout`, `DialKeepAliveTime`, `DialKeepAliveTimeout`, `MaxUnaryRetries`, `BackoffWaitBetween`, `BackoffJitterFraction`\\n- Default options in options.go:\\n  - `defaultUnaryMaxRetries = 100`: Max retries for unary calls\\n  - `defaultBackoffWaitBetween = 25ms`: Wait between retries\\n  - `defaultBackoffJitterFraction = 0.10`: 10% jitter\\n  - `defaultWaitForReady = true`: Wait for server readiness\\n- DialTimeout bounds connection setup\\n- MaxCallSendMsgSize and MaxCallRecvMsgSize configure message size limits\\n\\n## 9.
